8961: wine-shop worked like a manful soldier, Two fierce hours.
8962: 
8963: Deep ditch, single drawbridge, massive stone walls, eight great towers,
8964: cannon, muskets, fire and smoke. One drawbridge down! "Work, comrades
8965: all, work! Work, Jacques One, Jacques Two, Jacques One Thousand, Jacques
8966: Two Thousand, Jacques Five-and-Twenty Thousand; in the name of all
8967: the Angels or the Devils--which you prefer--work!" Thus Defarge of the
8968: wine-shop, still at his gun, which had long grown hot.
8969: 
8970: "To me, women!" cried madame his wife. "What! We can kill as well as
8971: the men when the place is taken!" And to her, with a shrill thirsty
8972: cry, trooping women variously armed, but all armed alike in hunger and
8973: revenge.
8974: 
8975: Cannon, muskets, fire and smoke; but, still the deep ditch, the single
8976: drawbridge, the massive stone walls, and the eight great towers. Slight
8977: displacements of the raging sea, made by the falling wounded. Flashing
8978: weapons, blazing torches, smoking waggonloads of wet straw, hard work
8979: at neighbouring barricades in all directions, shrieks, volleys,
8980: execrations, bravery without stint, boom smash and rattle, and the
8981: furious sounding of the living sea; but, still the deep ditch, and the
8982: single drawbridge, and the massive stone walls, and the eight great
8983: towers, and still Defarge of the wine-shop at his gun, grown doubly hot
8984: by the service of Four fierce hours.
8985: 
8986: A white flag from within the fortress, and a parley--this dimly
8987: perceptible through the raging storm, nothing audible in it--suddenly
8988: the sea rose immeasurably wider and higher, and swept Defarge of the
8989: wine-shop over the lowered drawbridge, past the massive stone outer
8990: walls, in among the eight great towers surrendered!
8991: 
8992: So resistless was the force of the ocean bearing him on, that even to
8993: draw his breath or turn his head was as impracticable as if he had been
8994: struggling in the surf at the South Sea, until he was landed in the
8995: outer courtyard of the Bastille. There, against an angle of a wall, he
8996: made a struggle to look about him. Jacques Three was nearly at his side;
8997: Madame Defarge, still heading some of her women, was visible in the
8998: inner distance, and her knife was in her hand. Everywhere was tumult,
8999: exultation, deafening and maniacal bewilderment, astounding noise, yet
9000: furious dumb-show.
9001: 
9002: "The Prisoners!"
9003: 
9004: "The Records!"
9005: 
9006: "The secret cells!"
9007: 
9008: "The instruments of torture!"
9009: 
9010: "The Prisoners!"
9011: 
9012: Of all these cries, and ten thousand incoherences, "The Prisoners!" was
9013: the cry most taken up by the sea that rushed in, as if there were an
9014: eternity of people, as well as of time and space. When the foremost
9015: billows rolled past, bearing the prison officers with them, and
9016: threatening them all with instant death if any secret nook remained
9017: undisclosed, Defarge laid his strong hand on the breast of one of
9018: these men--a man with a grey head, who had a lighted torch in his
9019: hand--separated him from the rest, and got him between himself and the
9020: wall.
9021: 
9022: "Show me the North Tower!" said Defarge. "Quick!"
9023: 
9024: "I will faithfully," replied the man, "if you will come with me. But
9025: there is no one there."
9026: 
9027: "What is the meaning of One Hundred and Five, North Tower?" asked
9028: Defarge. "Quick!"
9029: 
9030: "The meaning, monsieur?"
9031: 
9032: "Does it mean a captive, or a place of captivity? Or do you mean that I
9033: shall strike you dead?"
9034: 
9035: "Kill him!" croaked Jacques Three, who had come close up.
9036: 
9037: "Monsieur, it is a cell."
9038: 
9039: "Show it me!"
9040: 
9041: "Pass this way, then."
9042: 
9043: Jacques Three, with his usual craving on him, and evidently disappointed
9044: by the dialogue taking a turn that did not seem to promise bloodshed,
9045: held by Defarge's arm as he held by the turnkey's. Their three heads had
9046: been close together during this brief discourse, and it had been as much
9047: as they could do to hear one another, even then: so tremendous was the
9048: noise of the living ocean, in its irruption into the Fortress, and
9049: its inundation of the courts and passages and staircases. All around
9050: outside, too, it beat the walls with a deep, hoarse roar, from which,
9051: occasionally, some partial shouts of tumult broke and leaped into the
9052: air like spray.
9053: 
9054: Through gloomy vaults where the light of day had never shone, past
9055: hideous doors of dark dens and cages, down cavernous flights of steps,
9056: and again up steep rugged ascents of stone and brick, more like dry
9057: waterfalls than staircases, Defarge, the turnkey, and Jacques Three,
9058: linked hand and arm, went with all the speed they could make. Here and
9059: there, especially at first, the inundation started on them and swept by;
9060: but when they had done descending, and were winding and climbing up a
9061: tower, they were alone. Hemmed in here by the massive thickness of walls
9062: and arches, the storm within the fortress and without was only audible
9063: to them in a dull, subdued way, as if the noise out of which they had
9064: come had almost destroyed their sense of hearing.
9065: 
9066: The turnkey stopped at a low door, put a key in a clashing lock, swung
9067: the door slowly open, and said, as they all bent their heads and passed
9068: in:
9069: 
9070: "One hundred and five, North Tower!"
9071: 
9072: There was a small, heavily-grated, unglazed window high in the wall,
9073: with a stone screen before it, so that the sky could be only seen by
9074: stooping low and looking up. There was a small chimney, heavily barred
9075: across, a few feet within. There was a heap of old feathery wood-ashes
9076: on the hearth. There was a stool, and table, and a straw bed. There were
9077: the four blackened walls, and a rusted iron ring in one of them.
9078: 
9079: "Pass that torch slowly along these walls, that I may see them," said
9080: Defarge to the turnkey.
9081: 
9082: The man obeyed, and Defarge followed the light closely with his eyes.
9083: 
9084: "Stop!--Look here, Jacques!"
9085: 
9086: "A. M.!" croaked Jacques Three, as he read greedily.
9087: 
9088: "Alexandre Manette," said Defarge in his ear, following the letters
9089: with his swart forefinger, deeply engrained with gunpowder. "And here he
9090: wrote 'a poor physician.' And it was he, without doubt, who scratched
9091: a calendar on this stone. What is that in your hand? A crowbar? Give it
9092: me!"
9093: 
9094: He had still the linstock of his gun in his own hand. He made a sudden
9095: exchange of the two instruments, and turning on the worm-eaten stool and
9096: table, beat them to pieces in a few blows.
9097: 
9098: "Hold the light higher!" he said, wrathfully, to the turnkey. "Look
9099: among those fragments with care, Jacques. And see! Here is my knife,"
9100: throwing it to him; "rip open that bed, and search the straw. Hold the
9101: light higher, you!"
9102: 
9103: With a menacing look at the turnkey he crawled upon the hearth, and,
9104: peering up the chimney, struck and prised at its sides with the crowbar,
9105: and worked at the iron grating across it. In a few minutes, some mortar
9106: and dust came dropping down, which he averted his face to avoid; and
9107: in it, and in the old wood-ashes, and in a crevice in the chimney
9108: into which his weapon had slipped or wrought itself, he groped with a
9109: cautious touch.
9110: 
9111: "Nothing in the wood, and nothing in the straw, Jacques?"
9112: 
9113: "Nothing."
9114: 
9115: "Let us collect them together, in the middle of the cell. So! Light
9116: them, you!"
9117: 
9118: The turnkey fired the little pile, which blazed high and hot. Stooping
9119: again to come out at the low-arched door, they left it burning, and
9120: retraced their way to the courtyard; seeming to recover their sense
9121: of hearing as they came down, until they were in the raging flood once
9122: more.
9123: 
9124: They found it surging and tossing, in quest of Defarge himself. Saint
9125: Antoine was clamorous to have its wine-shop keeper foremost in the guard
9126: upon the governor who had defended the Bastille and shot the people.
9127: Otherwise, the governor would not be marched to the Hotel de Ville for
9128: judgment. Otherwise, the governor would escape, and the people's
9129: blood (suddenly of some value, after many years of worthlessness) be
9130: unavenged.
9131: 
9132: In the howling universe of passion and contention that seemed to
9133: encompass this grim old officer conspicuous in his grey coat and red
9134: decoration, there was but one quite steady figure, and that was a
9135: woman's. "See, there is my husband!" she cried, pointing him out.
9136: "See Defarge!" She stood immovable close to the grim old officer, and
9137: remained immovable close to him; remained immovable close to him through
9138: the streets, as Defarge and the rest bore him along; remained immovable
9139: close to him when he was got near his destination, and began to
9140: be struck at from behind; remained immovable close to him when the
9141: long-gathering rain of stabs and blows fell heavy; was so close to him
9142: when he dropped dead under it, that, suddenly animated, she put her foot
9143: upon his neck, and with her cruel knife--long ready--hewed off his head.
9144: 
9145: The hour was come, when Saint Antoine was to execute his horrible idea
9146: of hoisting up men for lamps to show what he could be and do. Saint
9147: Antoine's blood was up, and the blood of tyranny and domination by the
9148: iron hand was down--down on the steps of the Hotel de Ville where the
9149: governor's body lay--down on the sole of the shoe of Madame Defarge
9150: where she had trodden on the body to steady it for mutilation. "Lower
9151: the lamp yonder!" cried Saint Antoine, after glaring round for a new
9152: means of death; "here is one of his soldiers to be left on guard!" The
9153: swinging sentinel was posted, and the sea rushed on.
9154: 
9155: The sea of black and threatening waters, and of destructive upheaving
9156: of wave against wave, whose depths were yet unfathomed and whose forces
9157: were yet unknown. The remorseless sea of turbulently swaying shapes,
9158: voices of vengeance, and faces hardened in the furnaces of suffering
9159: until the touch of pity could make no mark on them.
9160: 
9161: But, in the ocean of faces where every fierce and furious expression was
9162: in vivid life, there were two groups of faces--each seven in number--so
9163: fixedly contrasting with the rest, that never did sea roll which bore
9164: more memorable wrecks with it. Seven faces of prisoners, suddenly
9165: released by the storm that had burst their tomb, were carried high
9166: overhead: all scared, all lost, all wondering and amazed, as if the Last
9167: Day were come, and those who rejoiced around them were lost spirits.
9168: Other seven faces there were, carried higher, seven dead faces, whose
9169: drooping eyelids and half-seen eyes awaited the Last Day. Impassive
9170: faces, yet with a suspended--not an abolished--expression on them;
9171: faces, rather, in a fearful pause, as having yet to raise the dropped
9172: lids of the eyes, and bear witness with the bloodless lips, "THOU DIDST
9173: IT!"
9174: 
9175: Seven prisoners released, seven gory heads on pikes, the keys of the
9176: accursed fortress of the eight strong towers, some discovered letters
9177: and other memorials of prisoners of old time, long dead of broken
9178: hearts,--such, and such--like, the loudly echoing footsteps of Saint
9179: Antoine escort through the Paris streets in mid-July, one thousand seven
9180: hundred and eighty-nine. Now, Heaven defeat the fancy of Lucie Darnay,
9181: and keep these feet far out of her life! For, they are headlong, mad,
9182: and dangerous; and in the years so long after the breaking of the cask
9183: at Defarge's wine-shop door, they are not easily purified when once
9184: stained red.
9185: 
9186: 
9187: 
9188: 
9189: XXII. The Sea Still Rises
9190: 
9191: 
9192: Haggard Saint Antoine had had only one exultant week, in which to soften
9193: his modicum of hard and bitter bread to such extent as he could, with
9194: the relish of fraternal embraces and congratulations, when Madame
9195: Defarge sat at her counter, as usual, presiding over the customers.
9196: Madame Defarge wore no rose in her head, for the great brotherhood of
9197: Spies had become, even in one short week, extremely chary of trusting
9198: themselves to the saint's mercies. The lamps across his streets had a
9199: portentously elastic swing with them.
9200: 
9201: Madame Defarge, with her arms folded, sat in the morning light and heat,
9202: contemplating the wine-shop and the street. In both, there were several
9203: knots of loungers, squalid and miserable, but now with a manifest sense
9204: of power enthroned on their distress. The raggedest nightcap, awry on
9205: the wretchedest head, had this crooked significance in it: "I know how
9206: hard it has grown for me, the wearer of this, to support life in myself;
9207: but do you know how easy it has grown for me, the wearer of this, to
9208: destroy life in you?" Every lean bare arm, that had been without work
9209: before, had this work always ready for it now, that it could strike.
9210: The fingers of the knitting women were vicious, with the experience that
9211: they could tear. There was a change in the appearance of Saint Antoine;
9212: the image had been hammering into this for hundreds of years, and the
9213: last finishing blows had told mightily on the expression.
9214: 
9215: Madame Defarge sat observing it, with such suppressed approval as was
9216: to be desired in the leader of the Saint Antoine women. One of her
9217: sisterhood knitted beside her. The short, rather plump wife of a starved
9218: grocer, and the mother of two children withal, this lieutenant had
9219: already earned the complimentary name of The Vengeance.
9220: 
9221: "Hark!" said The Vengeance. "Listen, then! Who comes?"
9222: 
9223: As if a train of powder laid from the outermost bound of Saint Antoine
9224: Quarter to the wine-shop door, had been suddenly fired, a fast-spreading
9225: murmur came rushing along.
9226: 
9227: "It is Defarge," said madame. "Silence, patriots!"
9228: 
9229: Defarge came in breathless, pulled off a red cap he wore, and looked
9230: around him! "Listen, everywhere!" said madame again. "Listen to him!"
9231: Defarge stood, panting, against a background of eager eyes and open
9232: mouths, formed outside the door; all those within the wine-shop had
9233: sprung to their feet.
9234: 
9235: "Say then, my husband. What is it?"
9236: 
9237: "News from the other world!"
9238: 
9239: "How, then?" cried madame, contemptuously. "The other world?"
9240: 
9241: "Does everybody here recall old Foulon, who told the famished people
9242: that they might eat grass, and who died, and went to Hell?"
9243: 
9244: "Everybody!" from all throats.
9245: 
9246: "The news is of him. He is among us!"
9247: 
9248: "Among us!" from the universal throat again. "And dead?"
9249: 
9250: "Not dead! He feared us so much--and with reason--that he caused himself
9251: to be represented as dead, and had a grand mock-funeral. But they have
9252: found him alive, hiding in the country, and have brought him in. I have
9253: seen him but now, on his way to the Hotel de Ville, a prisoner. I have
9254: said that he had reason to fear us. Say all! _Had_ he reason?"
9255: 
9256: Wretched old sinner of more than threescore years and ten, if he had
9257: never known it yet, he would have known it in his heart of hearts if he
9258: could have heard the answering cry.
9259: 
9260: A moment of profound silence followed. Defarge and his wife looked
9261: steadfastly at one another. The Vengeance stooped, and the jar of a drum
9262: was heard as she moved it at her feet behind the counter.
9263: 
9264: "Patriots!" said Defarge, in a determined voice, "are we ready?"
9265: 
9266: Instantly Madame Defarge's knife was in her girdle; the drum was beating
9267: in the streets, as if it and a drummer had flown together by magic; and
9268: The Vengeance, uttering terrific shrieks, and flinging her arms about
9269: her head like all the forty Furies at once, was tearing from house to
9270: house, rousing the women.
9271: 
9272: The men were terrible, in the bloody-minded anger with which they looked
9273: from windows, caught up what arms they had, and came pouring down into
9274: the streets; but, the women were a sight to chill the boldest. From
9275: such household occupations as their bare poverty yielded, from their
9276: children, from their aged and their sick crouching on the bare ground
9277: famished and naked, they ran out with streaming hair, urging one
9278: another, and themselves, to madness with the wildest cries and actions.
9279: Villain Foulon taken, my sister! Old Foulon taken, my mother! Miscreant
9280: Foulon taken, my daughter! Then, a score of others ran into the midst of
9281: these, beating their breasts, tearing their hair, and screaming, Foulon
9282: alive! Foulon who told the starving people they might eat grass! Foulon
9283: who told my old father that he might eat grass, when I had no bread
9284: to give him! Foulon who told my baby it might suck grass, when these
9285: breasts were dry with want! O mother of God, this Foulon! O Heaven our
9286: suffering! Hear me, my dead baby and my withered father: I swear on my
9287: knees, on these stones, to avenge you on Foulon! Husbands, and brothers,
9288: and young men, Give us the blood of Foulon, Give us the head of Foulon,
9289: Give us the heart of Foulon, Give us the body and soul of Foulon, Rend
9290: Foulon to pieces, and dig him into the ground, that grass may grow from
9291: him! With these cries, numbers of the women, lashed into blind frenzy,
9292: whirled about, striking and tearing at their own friends until they
9293: dropped into a passionate swoon, and were only saved by the men
9294: belonging to them from being trampled under foot.
9295: 
9296: Nevertheless, not a moment was lost; not a moment! This Foulon was at
9297: the Hotel de Ville, and might be loosed. Never, if Saint Antoine knew
9298: his own sufferings, insults, and wrongs! Armed men and women flocked out
9299: of the Quarter so fast, and drew even these last dregs after them with
9300: such a force of suction, that within a quarter of an hour there was not
9301: a human creature in Saint Antoine's bosom but a few old crones and the
9302: wailing children.
9303: 
9304: No. They were all by that time choking the Hall of Examination where
9305: this old man, ugly and wicked, was, and overflowing into the adjacent
9306: open space and streets. The Defarges, husband and wife, The Vengeance,
9307: and Jacques Three, were in the first press, and at no great distance
9308: from him in the Hall.
9309: 
9310: "See!" cried madame, pointing with her knife. "See the old villain bound
9311: with ropes. That was well done to tie a bunch of grass upon his back.
9312: Ha, ha! That was well done. Let him eat it now!" Madame put her knife
9313: under her arm, and clapped her hands as at a play.
9314: 
9315: The people immediately behind Madame Defarge, explaining the cause of
9316: her satisfaction to those behind them, and those again explaining to
9317: others, and those to others, the neighbouring streets resounded with the
9318: clapping of hands. Similarly, during two or three hours of drawl,
9319: and the winnowing of many bushels of words, Madame Defarge's frequent
9320: expressions of impatience were taken up, with marvellous quickness, at
9321: a distance: the more readily, because certain men who had by some
9322: wonderful exercise of agility climbed up the external architecture
9323: to look in from the windows, knew Madame Defarge well, and acted as a
9324: telegraph between her and the crowd outside the building.
9325: 
9326: At length the sun rose so high that it struck a kindly ray as of hope or
9327: protection, directly down upon the old prisoner's head. The favour was
9328: too much to bear; in an instant the barrier of dust and chaff that had
9329: stood surprisingly long, went to the winds, and Saint Antoine had got
9330: him!
9331: 
9332: It was known directly, to the furthest confines of the crowd. Defarge
9333: had but sprung over a railing and a table, and folded the miserable
9334: wretch in a deadly embrace--Madame Defarge had but followed and turned
9335: her hand in one of the ropes with which he was tied--The Vengeance and
9336: Jacques Three were not yet up with them, and the men at the windows
9337: had not yet swooped into the Hall, like birds of prey from their high
9338: perches--when the cry seemed to go up, all over the city, "Bring him
9339: out! Bring him to the lamp!"
9340: 
9341: Down, and up, and head foremost on the steps of the building; now, on
9342: his knees; now, on his feet; now, on his back; dragged, and struck at,
9343: and stifled by the bunches of grass and straw that were thrust into his
9344: face by hundreds of hands; torn, bruised, panting, bleeding, yet always
9345: entreating and beseeching for mercy; now full of vehement agony of
9346: action, with a small clear space about him as the people drew one
9347: another back that they might see; now, a log of dead wood drawn through
9348: a forest of legs; he was hauled to the nearest street corner where one
9349: of the fatal lamps swung, and there Madame Defarge let him go--as a cat
9350: might have done to a mouse--and silently and composedly looked at him
9351: while they made ready, and while he besought her: the women passionately
9352: screeching at him all the time, and the men sternly calling out to have
9353: him killed with grass in his mouth. Once, he went aloft, and the rope
9354: broke, and they caught him shrieking; twice, he went aloft, and the rope
9355: broke, and they caught him shrieking; then, the rope was merciful, and
9356: held him, and his head was soon upon a pike, with grass enough in the
9357: mouth for all Saint Antoine to dance at the sight of.
9358: 
9359: Nor was this the end of the day's bad work, for Saint Antoine so shouted
9360: and danced his angry blood up, that it boiled again, on hearing when
9361: the day closed in that the son-in-law of the despatched, another of the
9362: people's enemies and insulters, was coming into Paris under a guard
9363: five hundred strong, in cavalry alone. Saint Antoine wrote his crimes
9364: on flaring sheets of paper, seized him--would have torn him out of the
9365: breast of an army to bear Foulon company--set his head and heart on
9366: pikes, and carried the three spoils of the day, in Wolf-procession
9367: through the streets.
9368: 
9369: Not before dark night did the men and women come back to the children,
9370: wailing and breadless. Then, the miserable bakers' shops were beset by
9371: long files of them, patiently waiting to buy bad bread; and while
9372: they waited with stomachs faint and empty, they beguiled the time by
9373: embracing one another on the triumphs of the day, and achieving them
9374: again in gossip. Gradually, these strings of ragged people shortened and
9375: frayed away; and then poor lights began to shine in high windows, and
9376: slender fires were made in the streets, at which neighbours cooked in
9377: common, afterwards supping at their doors.
9378: 
9379: Scanty and insufficient suppers those, and innocent of meat, as of
9380: most other sauce to wretched bread. Yet, human fellowship infused
9381: some nourishment into the flinty viands, and struck some sparks of
9382: cheerfulness out of them. Fathers and mothers who had had their full
9383: share in the worst of the day, played gently with their meagre children;
9384: and lovers, with such a world around them and before them, loved and
9385: hoped.
9386: 
9387: It was almost morning, when Defarge's wine-shop parted with its last
9388: knot of customers, and Monsieur Defarge said to madame his wife, in
9389: husky tones, while fastening the door:
9390: 
9391: "At last it is come, my dear!"
9392: 
9393: "Eh well!" returned madame. "Almost."
9394: 
9395: Saint Antoine slept, the Defarges slept: even The Vengeance slept with
9396: her starved grocer, and the drum was at rest. The drum's was the
9397: only voice in Saint Antoine that blood and hurry had not changed. The
9398: Vengeance, as custodian of the drum, could have wakened him up and had
9399: the same speech out of him as before the Bastille fell, or old Foulon
9400: was seized; not so with the hoarse tones of the men and women in Saint
9401: Antoine's bosom.
9402: 
9403: 
9404: 
9405: 
9406: XXIII. Fire Rises
9407: 
9408: 
9409: There was a change on the village where the fountain fell, and where
9410: the mender of roads went forth daily to hammer out of the stones on the
9411: highway such morsels of bread as might serve for patches to hold his
9412: poor ignorant soul and his poor reduced body together. The prison on the
9413: crag was not so dominant as of yore; there were soldiers to guard it,
9414: but not many; there were officers to guard the soldiers, but not one of
9415: them knew what his men would do--beyond this: that it would probably not
9416: be what he was ordered.
9417: 
9418: Far and wide lay a ruined country, yielding nothing but desolation.
9419: Every green leaf, every blade of grass and blade of grain, was as
9420: shrivelled and poor as the miserable people. Everything was bowed down,
9421: dejected, oppressed, and broken. Habitations, fences, domesticated
9422: animals, men, women, children, and the soil that bore them--all worn
9423: out.
9424: 
9425: Monseigneur (often a most worthy individual gentleman) was a national
9426: blessing, gave a chivalrous tone to things, was a polite example of
9427: luxurious and shining life, and a great deal more to equal purpose;
9428: nevertheless, Monseigneur as a class had, somehow or other, brought
9429: things to this. Strange that Creation, designed expressly for
9430: Monseigneur, should be so soon wrung dry and squeezed out! There must
9431: be something short-sighted in the eternal arrangements, surely! Thus it
9432: was, however; and the last drop of blood having been extracted from the
9433: flints, and the last screw of the rack having been turned so often that
9434: its purchase crumbled, and it now turned and turned with nothing
9435: to bite, Monseigneur began to run away from a phenomenon so low and
9436: unaccountable.
9437: 
9438: But, this was not the change on the village, and on many a village like
9439: it. For scores of years gone by, Monseigneur had squeezed it and wrung
9440: it, and had seldom graced it with his presence except for the pleasures
9441: of the chase--now, found in hunting the people; now, found in hunting
9442: the beasts, for whose preservation Monseigneur made edifying spaces
9443: of barbarous and barren wilderness. No. The change consisted in
9444: the appearance of strange faces of low caste, rather than in the
9445: disappearance of the high caste, chiselled, and otherwise beautified and
9446: beautifying features of Monseigneur.
9447: 
9448: For, in these times, as the mender of roads worked, solitary, in the
9449: dust, not often troubling himself to reflect that dust he was and
9450: to dust he must return, being for the most part too much occupied in
9451: thinking how little he had for supper and how much more he would eat if
9452: he had it--in these times, as he raised his eyes from his lonely labour,
9453: and viewed the prospect, he would see some rough figure approaching on
9454: foot, the like of which was once a rarity in those parts, but was now
9455: a frequent presence. As it advanced, the mender of roads would discern
9456: without surprise, that it was a shaggy-haired man, of almost barbarian
9457: aspect, tall, in wooden shoes that were clumsy even to the eyes of a
9458: mender of roads, grim, rough, swart, steeped in the mud and dust of many
9459: highways, dank with the marshy moisture of many low grounds, sprinkled
9460: with the thorns and leaves and moss of many byways through woods.
9461: 
9462: Such a man came upon him, like a ghost, at noon in the July weather,
9463: as he sat on his heap of stones under a bank, taking such shelter as he
9464: could get from a shower of hail.
9465: 
9466: The man looked at him, looked at the village in the hollow, at the mill,
9467: and at the prison on the crag. When he had identified these objects
9468: in what benighted mind he had, he said, in a dialect that was just
9469: intelligible:
9470: 
9471: "How goes it, Jacques?"
9472: 
9473: "All well, Jacques."
9474: 
9475: "Touch then!"
9476: 
9477: They joined hands, and the man sat down on the heap of stones.
9478: 
9479: "No dinner?"
9480: 
9481: "Nothing but supper now," said the mender of roads, with a hungry face.
9482: 
9483: "It is the fashion," growled the man. "I meet no dinner anywhere."
9484: 
9485: He took out a blackened pipe, filled it, lighted it with flint and
9486: steel, pulled at it until it was in a bright glow: then, suddenly held
9487: it from him and dropped something into it from between his finger and
9488: thumb, that blazed and went out in a puff of smoke.
9489: 
9490: "Touch then." It was the turn of the mender of roads to say it this
9491: time, after observing these operations. They again joined hands.
9492: 
9493: "To-night?" said the mender of roads.
9494: 
9495: "To-night," said the man, putting the pipe in his mouth.
9496: 
9497: "Where?"
9498: 
9499: "Here."
9500: 
9501: He and the mender of roads sat on the heap of stones looking silently at
9502: one another, with the hail driving in between them like a pigmy charge
9503: of bayonets, until the sky began to clear over the village.
9504: 
9505: "Show me!" said the traveller then, moving to the brow of the hill.
9506: 
9507: "See!" returned the mender of roads, with extended finger. "You go down
9508: here, and straight through the street, and past the fountain--"
9509: 
9510: "To the Devil with all that!" interrupted the other, rolling his eye
9511: over the landscape. "_I_ go through no streets and past no fountains.
9512: Well?"
9513: 
9514: "Well! About two leagues beyond the summit of that hill above the
9515: village."
9516: 
9517: "Good. When do you cease to work?"
9518: 
9519: "At sunset."
9520: 
9521: "Will you wake me, before departing? I have walked two nights without
9522: resting. Let me finish my pipe, and I shall sleep like a child. Will you
9523: wake me?"
9524: 
9525: "Surely."
9526: 
9527: The wayfarer smoked his pipe out, put it in his breast, slipped off his
9528: great wooden shoes, and lay down on his back on the heap of stones. He
9529: was fast asleep directly.
9530: 
9531: As the road-mender plied his dusty labour, and the hail-clouds, rolling
9532: away, revealed bright bars and streaks of sky which were responded to
9533: by silver gleams upon the landscape, the little man (who wore a red cap
9534: now, in place of his blue one) seemed fascinated by the figure on the
9535: heap of stones. His eyes were so often turned towards it, that he used
9536: his tools mechanically, and, one would have said, to very poor account.
9537: The bronze face, the shaggy black hair and beard, the coarse woollen
9538: red cap, the rough medley dress of home-spun stuff and hairy skins of
9539: beasts, the powerful frame attenuated by spare living, and the sullen
9540: and desperate compression of the lips in sleep, inspired the mender
9541: of roads with awe. The traveller had travelled far, and his feet were
9542: footsore, and his ankles chafed and bleeding; his great shoes, stuffed
9543: with leaves and grass, had been heavy to drag over the many long
9544: leagues, and his clothes were chafed into holes, as he himself was into
9545: sores. Stooping down beside him, the road-mender tried to get a peep at
9546: secret weapons in his breast or where not; but, in vain, for he slept
9547: with his arms crossed upon him, and set as resolutely as his lips.
9548: Fortified towns with their stockades, guard-houses, gates, trenches, and
9549: drawbridges, seemed to the mender of roads, to be so much air as against
9550: this figure. And when he lifted his eyes from it to the horizon and
9551: looked around, he saw in his small fancy similar figures, stopped by no
9552: obstacle, tending to centres all over France.
9553: 
9554: The man slept on, indifferent to showers of hail and intervals of
9555: brightness, to sunshine on his face and shadow, to the paltering lumps
9556: of dull ice on his body and the diamonds into which the sun changed
9557: them, until the sun was low in the west, and the sky was glowing. Then,
9558: the mender of roads having got his tools together and all things ready
9559: to go down into the village, roused him.
9560: 
9561: "Good!" said the sleeper, rising on his elbow. "Two leagues beyond the
9562: summit of the hill?"
9563: 
9564: "About."
9565: 
9566: "About. Good!"
9567: 
9568: The mender of roads went home, with the dust going on before him
9569: according to the set of the wind, and was soon at the fountain,
9570: squeezing himself in among the lean kine brought there to drink, and
9571: appearing even to whisper to them in his whispering to all the village.
9572: When the village had taken its poor supper, it did not creep to bed,
9573: as it usually did, but came out of doors again, and remained there. A
9574: curious contagion of whispering was upon it, and also, when it gathered
9575: together at the fountain in the dark, another curious contagion of
9576: looking expectantly at the sky in one direction only. Monsieur Gabelle,
9577: chief functionary of the place, became uneasy; went out on his house-top
9578: alone, and looked in that direction too; glanced down from behind his
9579: chimneys at the darkening faces by the fountain below, and sent word to
9580: the sacristan who kept the keys of the church, that there might be need
9581: to ring the tocsin by-and-bye.
9582: 
9583: The night deepened. The trees environing the old chateau, keeping its
9584: solitary state apart, moved in a rising wind, as though they threatened
9585: the pile of building massive and dark in the gloom. Up the two terrace
9586: flights of steps the rain ran wildly, and beat at the great door, like a
9587: swift messenger rousing those within; uneasy rushes of wind went through
9588: the hall, among the old spears and knives, and passed lamenting up the
9589: stairs, and shook the curtains of the bed where the last Marquis
9590: had slept. East, West, North, and South, through the woods, four
9591: heavy-treading, unkempt figures crushed the high grass and cracked the
9592: branches, striding on cautiously to come together in the courtyard. Four
9593: lights broke out there, and moved away in different directions, and all
9594: was black again.
9595: 
9596: But, not for long. Presently, the chateau began to make itself strangely
9597: visible by some light of its own, as though it were growing luminous.
9598: Then, a flickering streak played behind the architecture of the front,
9599: picking out transparent places, and showing where balustrades, arches,
9600: and windows were. Then it soared higher, and grew broader and brighter.
9601: Soon, from a score of the great windows, flames burst forth, and the
9602: stone faces awakened, stared out of fire.
9603: 
9604: A faint murmur arose about the house from the few people who were left
9605: there, and there was a saddling of a horse and riding away. There was
9606: spurring and splashing through the darkness, and bridle was drawn in the
9607: space by the village fountain, and the horse in a foam stood at Monsieur
9608: Gabelle's door. "Help, Gabelle! Help, every one!" The tocsin rang
9609: impatiently, but other help (if that were any) there was none. The
9610: mender of roads, and two hundred and fifty particular friends, stood
9611: with folded arms at the fountain, looking at the pillar of fire in the
9612: sky. "It must be forty feet high," said they, grimly; and never moved.
9613: 
9614: The rider from the chateau, and the horse in a foam, clattered away
9615: through the village, and galloped up the stony steep, to the prison on
9616: the crag. At the gate, a group of officers were looking at the fire;
9617: removed from them, a group of soldiers. "Help, gentlemen--officers! The
9618: chateau is on fire; valuable objects may be saved from the flames by
9619: timely aid! Help, help!" The officers looked towards the soldiers who
9620: looked at the fire; gave no orders; and answered, with shrugs and biting
9621: of lips, "It must burn."
9622: 
9623: As the rider rattled down the hill again and through the street, the
9624: village was illuminating. The mender of roads, and the two hundred and
9625: fifty particular friends, inspired as one man and woman by the idea of
9626: lighting up, had darted into their houses, and were putting candles in
9627: every dull little pane of glass. The general scarcity of everything,
9628: occasioned candles to be borrowed in a rather peremptory manner of
9629: Monsieur Gabelle; and in a moment of reluctance and hesitation on
9630: that functionary's part, the mender of roads, once so submissive to
9631: authority, had remarked that carriages were good to make bonfires with,
9632: and that post-horses would roast.
9633: 
9634: The chateau was left to itself to flame and burn. In the roaring and
9635: raging of the conflagration, a red-hot wind, driving straight from the
9636: infernal regions, seemed to be blowing the edifice away. With the rising
9637: and falling of the blaze, the stone faces showed as if they were in
9638: torment. When great masses of stone and timber fell, the face with the
9639: two dints in the nose became obscured: anon struggled out of the smoke
9640: again, as if it were the face of the cruel Marquis, burning at the stake
9641: and contending with the fire.
9642: 
9643: The chateau burned; the nearest trees, laid hold of by the fire,
9644: scorched and shrivelled; trees at a distance, fired by the four fierce
9645: figures, begirt the blazing edifice with a new forest of smoke. Molten
9646: lead and iron boiled in the marble basin of the fountain; the water ran
9647: dry; the extinguisher tops of the towers vanished like ice before the
9648: heat, and trickled down into four rugged wells of flame. Great rents and
9649: splits branched out in the solid walls, like crystallisation; stupefied
9650: birds wheeled about and dropped into the furnace; four fierce figures
9651: trudged away, East, West, North, and South, along the night-enshrouded
9652: roads, guided by the beacon they had lighted, towards their next
9653: destination. The illuminated village had seized hold of the tocsin, and,
9654: abolishing the lawful ringer, rang for joy.
9655: 
9656: Not only that; but the village, light-headed with famine, fire, and
9657: bell-ringing, and bethinking itself that Monsieur Gabelle had to do with
9658: the collection of rent and taxes--though it was but a small instalment
9659: of taxes, and no rent at all, that Gabelle had got in those latter
9660: days--became impatient for an interview with him, and, surrounding his
9661: house, summoned him to come forth for personal conference. Whereupon,
9662: Monsieur Gabelle did heavily bar his door, and retire to hold counsel
9663: with himself. The result of that conference was, that Gabelle again
9664: withdrew himself to his housetop behind his stack of chimneys; this time
9665: resolved, if his door were broken in (he was a small Southern man
9666: of retaliative temperament), to pitch himself head foremost over the
9667: parapet, and crush a man or two below.
9668: 
9669: Probably, Monsieur Gabelle passed a long night up there, with the
9670: distant chateau for fire and candle, and the beating at his door,
9671: combined with the joy-ringing, for music; not to mention his having an
9672: ill-omened lamp slung across the road before his posting-house gate,
9673: which the village showed a lively inclination to displace in his favour.
9674: A trying suspense, to be passing a whole summer night on the brink of
9675: the black ocean, ready to take that plunge into it upon which Monsieur
9676: Gabelle had resolved! But, the friendly dawn appearing at last, and the
9677: rush-candles of the village guttering out, the people happily dispersed,
9678: and Monsieur Gabelle came down bringing his life with him for that
9679: while.
9680: 
9681: Within a hundred miles, and in the light of other fires, there were
9682: other functionaries less fortunate, that night and other nights, whom
9683: the rising sun found hanging across once-peaceful streets, where they
9684: had been born and bred; also, there were other villagers and townspeople
9685: less fortunate than the mender of roads and his fellows, upon whom the
9686: functionaries and soldiery turned with success, and whom they strung up
9687: in their turn. But, the fierce figures were steadily wending East, West,
9688: North, and South, be that as it would; and whosoever hung, fire burned.
9689: The altitude of the gallows that would turn to water and quench it,
9690: no functionary, by any stretch of mathematics, was able to calculate
9691: successfully.
9692: 
9693: 
9694: 
9695: 
9696: XXIV. Drawn to the Loadstone Rock
9697: 
9698: 
9699: In such risings of fire and risings of sea--the firm earth shaken by
9700: the rushes of an angry ocean which had now no ebb, but was always on the
9701: flow, higher and higher, to the terror and wonder of the beholders on
9702: the shore--three years of tempest were consumed. Three more birthdays
9703: of little Lucie had been woven by the golden thread into the peaceful
9704: tissue of the life of her home.
9705: 
9706: Many a night and many a day had its inmates listened to the echoes in
9707: the corner, with hearts that failed them when they heard the thronging
9708: feet. For, the footsteps had become to their minds as the footsteps of
9709: a people, tumultuous under a red flag and with their country declared in
9710: danger, changed into wild beasts, by terrible enchantment long persisted
9711: in.
9712: 
9713: Monseigneur, as a class, had dissociated himself from the phenomenon of
9714: his not being appreciated: of his being so little wanted in France, as
9715: to incur considerable danger of receiving his dismissal from it, and
9716: this life together. Like the fabled rustic who raised the Devil with
9717: infinite pains, and was so terrified at the sight of him that he could
9718: ask the Enemy no question, but immediately fled; so, Monseigneur, after
9719: boldly reading the Lord's Prayer backwards for a great number of years,
9720: and performing many other potent spells for compelling the Evil One, no
9721: sooner beheld him in his terrors than he took to his noble heels.
9722: 
9723: The shining Bull's Eye of the Court was gone, or it would have been the
9724: mark for a hurricane of national bullets. It had never been a good
9725: eye to see with--had long had the mote in it of Lucifer's pride,
9726: Sardanapalus's luxury, and a mole's blindness--but it had dropped
9727: out and was gone. The Court, from that exclusive inner circle to its
9728: outermost rotten ring of intrigue, corruption, and dissimulation, was
9729: all gone together. Royalty was gone; had been besieged in its Palace and
9730: "suspended," when the last tidings came over.
9731: 
9732: The August of the year one thousand seven hundred and ninety-two was
9733: come, and Monseigneur was by this time scattered far and wide.
9734: 
9735: As was natural, the head-quarters and great gathering-place of
9736: Monseigneur, in London, was Tellson's Bank. Spirits are supposed to
9737: haunt the places where their bodies most resorted, and Monseigneur
9738: without a guinea haunted the spot where his guineas used to be.
9739: Moreover, it was the spot to which such French intelligence as was most
9740: to be relied upon, came quickest. Again: Tellson's was a munificent
9741: house, and extended great liberality to old customers who had fallen
9742: from their high estate. Again: those nobles who had seen the coming
9743: storm in time, and anticipating plunder or confiscation, had made
9744: provident remittances to Tellson's, were always to be heard of there
9745: by their needy brethren. To which it must be added that every new-comer
9746: from France reported himself and his tidings at Tellson's, almost as
9747: a matter of course. For such variety of reasons, Tellson's was at that
9748: time, as to French intelligence, a kind of High Exchange; and this
9749: was so well known to the public, and the inquiries made there were in
9750: consequence so numerous, that Tellson's sometimes wrote the latest news
9751: out in a line or so and posted it in the Bank windows, for all who ran
9752: through Temple Bar to read.
9753: 
9754: On a steaming, misty afternoon, Mr. Lorry sat at his desk, and Charles
9755: Darnay stood leaning on it, talking with him in a low voice. The
9756: penitential den once set apart for interviews with the House, was now
9757: the news-Exchange, and was filled to overflowing. It was within half an
9758: hour or so of the time of closing.
9759: 
9760: "But, although you are the youngest man that ever lived," said Charles
9761: Darnay, rather hesitating, "I must still suggest to you--"
9762: 
9763: "I understand. That I am too old?" said Mr. Lorry.
9764: 
9765: "Unsettled weather, a long journey, uncertain means of travelling, a
9766: disorganised country, a city that may not be even safe for you."
9767: 
9768: "My dear Charles," said Mr. Lorry, with cheerful confidence, "you touch
9769: some of the reasons for my going: not for my staying away. It is safe
9770: enough for me; nobody will care to interfere with an old fellow of hard
9771: upon fourscore when there are so many people there much better worth
9772: interfering with. As to its being a disorganised city, if it were not a
9773: disorganised city there would be no occasion to send somebody from our
9774: House here to our House there, who knows the city and the business, of
9775: old, and is in Tellson's confidence. As to the uncertain travelling, the
9776: long journey, and the winter weather, if I were not prepared to submit
9777: myself to a few inconveniences for the sake of Tellson's, after all
9778: these years, who ought to be?"
9779: 
9780: "I wish I were going myself," said Charles Darnay, somewhat restlessly,
9781: and like one thinking aloud.
9782: 
9783: "Indeed! You are a pretty fellow to object and advise!" exclaimed Mr.
9784: Lorry. "You wish you were going yourself? And you a Frenchman born? You
9785: are a wise counsellor."
9786: 
9787: "My dear Mr. Lorry, it is because I am a Frenchman born, that the
9788: thought (which I did not mean to utter here, however) has passed through
9789: my mind often. One cannot help thinking, having had some sympathy for
9790: the miserable people, and having abandoned something to them," he spoke
9791: here in his former thoughtful manner, "that one might be listened to,
9792: and might have the power to persuade to some restraint. Only last night,
9793: after you had left us, when I was talking to Lucie--"
9794: 
9795: "When you were talking to Lucie," Mr. Lorry repeated. "Yes. I wonder you
9796: are not ashamed to mention the name of Lucie! Wishing you were going to
9797: France at this time of day!"
9798: 
9799: "However, I am not going," said Charles Darnay, with a smile. "It is
9800: more to the purpose that you say you are."
9801: 
9802: "And I am, in plain reality. The truth is, my dear Charles," Mr. Lorry
9803: glanced at the distant House, and lowered his voice, "you can have no
9804: conception of the difficulty with which our business is transacted, and
9805: of the peril in which our books and papers over yonder are involved. The
9806: Lord above knows what the compromising consequences would be to numbers
9807: of people, if some of our documents were seized or destroyed; and they
9808: might be, at any time, you know, for who can say that Paris is not set
9809: afire to-day, or sacked to-morrow! Now, a judicious selection from these
9810: with the least possible delay, and the burying of them, or otherwise
9811: getting of them out of harm's way, is within the power (without loss of
9812: precious time) of scarcely any one but myself, if any one. And shall
9813: I hang back, when Tellson's knows this and says this--Tellson's, whose
9814: bread I have eaten these sixty years--because I am a little stiff about
9815: the joints? Why, I am a boy, sir, to half a dozen old codgers here!"
9816: 
9817: "How I admire the gallantry of your youthful spirit, Mr. Lorry."
9818: 
9819: "Tut! Nonsense, sir!--And, my dear Charles," said Mr. Lorry, glancing at
9820: the House again, "you are to remember, that getting things out of
9821: Paris at this present time, no matter what things, is next to an
9822: impossibility. Papers and precious matters were this very day brought
9823: to us here (I speak in strict confidence; it is not business-like to
9824: whisper it, even to you), by the strangest bearers you can imagine,
9825: every one of whom had his head hanging on by a single hair as he passed
9826: the Barriers. At another time, our parcels would come and go, as easily
9827: as in business-like Old England; but now, everything is stopped."
9828: 
9829: "And do you really go to-night?"
9830: 
9831: "I really go to-night, for the case has become too pressing to admit of
9832: delay."
9833: 
9834: "And do you take no one with you?"
9835: 
9836: "All sorts of people have been proposed to me, but I will have nothing
9837: to say to any of them. I intend to take Jerry. Jerry has been my
9838: bodyguard on Sunday nights for a long time past and I am used to him.
9839: Nobody will suspect Jerry of being anything but an English bull-dog, or
9840: of having any design in his head but to fly at anybody who touches his
9841: master."
9842: 
9843: "I must say again that I heartily admire your gallantry and
9844: youthfulness."
9845: 
9846: "I must say again, nonsense, nonsense! When I have executed this little
9847: commission, I shall, perhaps, accept Tellson's proposal to retire and
9848: live at my ease. Time enough, then, to think about growing old."
9849: 
9850: This dialogue had taken place at Mr. Lorry's usual desk, with
9851: Monseigneur swarming within a yard or two of it, boastful of what he
9852: would do to avenge himself on the rascal-people before long. It was too
9853: much the way of Monseigneur under his reverses as a refugee, and it
9854: was much too much the way of native British orthodoxy, to talk of this
9855: terrible Revolution as if it were the only harvest ever known under
9856: the skies that had not been sown--as if nothing had ever been done, or
9857: omitted to be done, that had led to it--as if observers of the wretched
9858: millions in France, and of the misused and perverted resources that
9859: should have made them prosperous, had not seen it inevitably coming,
9860: years before, and had not in plain words recorded what they saw. Such
9861: vapouring, combined with the extravagant plots of Monseigneur for the
9862: restoration of a state of things that had utterly exhausted itself,
9863: and worn out Heaven and earth as well as itself, was hard to be endured
9864: without some remonstrance by any sane man who knew the truth. And it was
9865: such vapouring all about his ears, like a troublesome confusion of blood
9866: in his own head, added to a latent uneasiness in his mind, which had
9867: already made Charles Darnay restless, and which still kept him so.
9868: 
9869: Among the talkers, was Stryver, of the King's Bench Bar, far on his
9870: way to state promotion, and, therefore, loud on the theme: broaching
9871: to Monseigneur, his devices for blowing the people up and exterminating
9872: them from the face of the earth, and doing without them: and for
9873: accomplishing many similar objects akin in their nature to the abolition
9874: of eagles by sprinkling salt on the tails of the race. Him, Darnay heard
9875: with a particular feeling of objection; and Darnay stood divided between
9876: going away that he might hear no more, and remaining to interpose his
9877: word, when the thing that was to be, went on to shape itself out.
9878: 
9879: The House approached Mr. Lorry, and laying a soiled and unopened letter
9880: before him, asked if he had yet discovered any traces of the person to
9881: whom it was addressed? The House laid the letter down so close to Darnay
9882: that he saw the direction--the more quickly because it was his own right
9883: name. The address, turned into English, ran:
9884: 
9885: "Very pressing. To Monsieur heretofore the Marquis St. Evremonde, of
9886: France. Confided to the cares of Messrs. Tellson and Co., Bankers,
9887: London, England."
9888: 
9889: On the marriage morning, Doctor Manette had made it his one urgent and
9890: express request to Charles Darnay, that the secret of this name should
9891: be--unless he, the Doctor, dissolved the obligation--kept inviolate
9892: between them. Nobody else knew it to be his name; his own wife had no
9893: suspicion of the fact; Mr. Lorry could have none.
9894: 
9895: "No," said Mr. Lorry, in reply to the House; "I have referred it,
9896: I think, to everybody now here, and no one can tell me where this
9897: gentleman is to be found."
9898: 
9899: The hands of the clock verging upon the hour of closing the Bank, there
9900: was a general set of the current of talkers past Mr. Lorry's desk. He
9901: held the letter out inquiringly; and Monseigneur looked at it, in the
9902: person of this plotting and indignant refugee; and Monseigneur looked at
9903: it in the person of that plotting and indignant refugee; and This, That,
9904: and The Other, all had something disparaging to say, in French or in
9905: English, concerning the Marquis who was not to be found.
9906: 
9907: "Nephew, I believe--but in any case degenerate successor--of the
9908: polished Marquis who was murdered," said one. "Happy to say, I never
9909: knew him."
9910: 
9911: "A craven who abandoned his post," said another--this Monseigneur had
9912: been got out of Paris, legs uppermost and half suffocated, in a load of
9913: hay--"some years ago."
9914: 
9915: "Infected with the new doctrines," said a third, eyeing the direction
9916: through his glass in passing; "set himself in opposition to the last
9917: Marquis, abandoned the estates when he inherited them, and left them to
9918: the ruffian herd. They will recompense him now, I hope, as he deserves."
9919: 
9920: "Hey?" cried the blatant Stryver. "Did he though? Is that the sort of
9921: fellow? Let us look at his infamous name. D--n the fellow!"
9922: 
9923: Darnay, unable to restrain himself any longer, touched Mr. Stryver on
9924: the shoulder, and said:
9925: 
9926: "I know the fellow."
9927: 
9928: "Do you, by Jupiter?" said Stryver. "I am sorry for it."
9929: 
9930: "Why?"
9931: 
9932: "Why, Mr. Darnay? D'ye hear what he did? Don't ask, why, in these
9933: times."
9934: 
9935: "But I do ask why?"
9936: 
9937: "Then I tell you again, Mr. Darnay, I am sorry for it. I am sorry to
9938: hear you putting any such extraordinary questions. Here is a fellow,
9939: who, infected by the most pestilent and blasphemous code of devilry that
9940: ever was known, abandoned his property to the vilest scum of the earth
9941: that ever did murder by wholesale, and you ask me why I am sorry that a
9942: man who instructs youth knows him? Well, but I'll answer you. I am sorry
9943: because I believe there is contamination in such a scoundrel. That's
9944: why."
9945: 
9946: Mindful of the secret, Darnay with great difficulty checked himself, and
9947: said: "You may not understand the gentleman."
9948: 
9949: "I understand how to put _you_ in a corner, Mr. Darnay," said Bully
9950: Stryver, "and I'll do it. If this fellow is a gentleman, I _don't_
9951: understand him. You may tell him so, with my compliments. You may also
9952: tell him, from me, that after abandoning his worldly goods and position
9953: to this butcherly mob, I wonder he is not at the head of them. But, no,
9954: gentlemen," said Stryver, looking all round, and snapping his fingers,
9955: "I know something of human nature, and I tell you that you'll never
9956: find a fellow like this fellow, trusting himself to the mercies of such
9957: precious _proteges_. No, gentlemen; he'll always show 'em a clean pair
9958: of heels very early in the scuffle, and sneak away."
9959: 
9960: With those words, and a final snap of his fingers, Mr. Stryver
9961: shouldered himself into Fleet-street, amidst the general approbation of
9962: his hearers. Mr. Lorry and Charles Darnay were left alone at the desk,
9963: in the general departure from the Bank.
9964: 
9965: "Will you take charge of the letter?" said Mr. Lorry. "You know where to
9966: deliver it?"
9967: 
9968: "I do."
9969: 
9970: "Will you undertake to explain, that we suppose it to have been
9971: addressed here, on the chance of our knowing where to forward it, and
9972: that it has been here some time?"
9973: 
9974: "I will do so. Do you start for Paris from here?"
9975: 
9976: "From here, at eight."
9977: 
9978: "I will come back, to see you off."
9979: 
9980: Very ill at ease with himself, and with Stryver and most other men,
9981: Darnay made the best of his way into the quiet of the Temple, opened the
9982: letter, and read it. These were its contents:
9983: 
9984: 
9985: "Prison of the Abbaye, Paris.
9986: 
9987: "June 21, 1792. "MONSIEUR HERETOFORE THE MARQUIS.
9988: 
9989: "After having long been in danger of my life at the hands of the
9990: village, I have been seized, with great violence and indignity, and
9991: brought a long journey on foot to Paris. On the road I have suffered a
9992: great deal. Nor is that all; my house has been destroyed--razed to the
9993: ground.
9994: 
9995: "The crime for which I am imprisoned, Monsieur heretofore the Marquis,
9996: and for which I shall be summoned before the tribunal, and shall lose my
9997: life (without your so generous help), is, they tell me, treason against
9998: the majesty of the people, in that I have acted against them for an
9999: emigrant. It is in vain I represent that I have acted for them, and not
10000: against, according to your commands. It is in vain I represent that,
10001: before the sequestration of emigrant property, I had remitted the
10002: imposts they had ceased to pay; that I had collected no rent; that I had
10003: had recourse to no process. The only response is, that I have acted for
10004: an emigrant, and where is that emigrant?
10005: 
10006: "Ah! most gracious Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, where is that
10007: emigrant? I cry in my sleep where is he? I demand of Heaven, will he
10008: not come to deliver me? No answer. Ah Monsieur heretofore the Marquis,
10009: I send my desolate cry across the sea, hoping it may perhaps reach your
10010: ears through the great bank of Tilson known at Paris!
10011: 
10012: "For the love of Heaven, of justice, of generosity, of the honour of
10013: your noble name, I supplicate you, Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, to
10014: succour and release me. My fault is, that I have been true to you. Oh
10015: Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, I pray you be you true to me!
10016: 
10017: "From this prison here of horror, whence I every hour tend nearer and
10018: nearer to destruction, I send you, Monsieur heretofore the Marquis, the
10019: assurance of my dolorous and unhappy service.
10020: 
10021: "Your afflicted,
10022: 
10023: "Gabelle."
10024: 
10025: 
10026: The latent uneasiness in Darnay's mind was roused to vigourous life
10027: by this letter. The peril of an old servant and a good one, whose
10028: only crime was fidelity to himself and his family, stared him so
10029: reproachfully in the face, that, as he walked to and fro in the Temple
10030: considering what to do, he almost hid his face from the passersby.
10031: 
10032: He knew very well, that in his horror of the deed which had culminated
10033: the bad deeds and bad reputation of the old family house, in his
10034: resentful suspicions of his uncle, and in the aversion with which his
10035: conscience regarded the crumbling fabric that he was supposed to uphold,
10036: he had acted imperfectly. He knew very well, that in his love for Lucie,
10037: his renunciation of his social place, though by no means new to his own
10038: mind, had been hurried and incomplete. He knew that he ought to have
10039: systematically worked it out and supervised it, and that he had meant to
10040: do it, and that it had never been done.
10041: 
10042: The happiness of his own chosen English home, the necessity of being
10043: always actively employed, the swift changes and troubles of the time
10044: which had followed on one another so fast, that the events of this week
10045: annihilated the immature plans of last week, and the events of the week
10046: following made all new again; he knew very well, that to the force of
10047: these circumstances he had yielded:--not without disquiet, but still
10048: without continuous and accumulating resistance. That he had watched
10049: the times for a time of action, and that they had shifted and struggled
10050: until the time had gone by, and the nobility were trooping from
10051: France by every highway and byway, and their property was in course of
10052: confiscation and destruction, and their very names were blotting out,
10053: was as well known to himself as it could be to any new authority in
10054: France that might impeach him for it.
10055: 
10056: But, he had oppressed no man, he had imprisoned no man; he was so
10057: far from having harshly exacted payment of his dues, that he had
10058: relinquished them of his own will, thrown himself on a world with no
10059: favour in it, won his own private place there, and earned his own
10060: bread. Monsieur Gabelle had held the impoverished and involved estate
10061: on written instructions, to spare the people, to give them what little
10062: there was to give--such fuel as the heavy creditors would let them have
10063: in the winter, and such produce as could be saved from the same grip in
10064: the summer--and no doubt he had put the fact in plea and proof, for his
10065: own safety, so that it could not but appear now.
10066: 
10067: This favoured the desperate resolution Charles Darnay had begun to make,
10068: that he would go to Paris.
10069: 
10070: Yes. Like the mariner in the old story, the winds and streams had driven
10071: him within the influence of the Loadstone Rock, and it was drawing him
10072: to itself, and he must go. Everything that arose before his mind drifted
10073: him on, faster and faster, more and more steadily, to the terrible
10074: attraction. His latent uneasiness had been, that bad aims were being
10075: worked out in his own unhappy land by bad instruments, and that he who
10076: could not fail to know that he was better than they, was not there,
10077: trying to do something to stay bloodshed, and assert the claims of mercy
10078: and humanity. With this uneasiness half stifled, and half reproaching
10079: him, he had been brought to the pointed comparison of himself with the
10080: brave old gentleman in whom duty was so strong; upon that comparison
10081: (injurious to himself) had instantly followed the sneers of Monseigneur,
10082: which had stung him bitterly, and those of Stryver, which above all were
10083: coarse and galling, for old reasons. Upon those, had followed Gabelle's
10084: letter: the appeal of an innocent prisoner, in danger of death, to his
10085: justice, honour, and good name.
10086: 
10087: His resolution was made. He must go to Paris.
10088: 
10089: Yes. The Loadstone Rock was drawing him, and he must sail on, until he
10090: struck. He knew of no rock; he saw hardly any danger. The intention
10091: with which he had done what he had done, even although he had left
10092: it incomplete, presented it before him in an aspect that would be
10093: gratefully acknowledged in France on his presenting himself to assert
10094: it. Then, that glorious vision of doing good, which is so often the
10095: sanguine mirage of so many good minds, arose before him, and he even
10096: saw himself in the illusion with some influence to guide this raging
10097: Revolution that was running so fearfully wild.
10098: 
10099: As he walked to and fro with his resolution made, he considered that
10100: neither Lucie nor her father must know of it until he was gone.
10101: Lucie should be spared the pain of separation; and her father, always
10102: reluctant to turn his thoughts towards the dangerous ground of old,
10103: should come to the knowledge of the step, as a step taken, and not in
10104: the balance of suspense and doubt. How much of the incompleteness of his
10105: situation was referable to her father, through the painful anxiety
10106: to avoid reviving old associations of France in his mind, he did not
10107: discuss with himself. But, that circumstance too, had had its influence
10108: in his course.
10109: 
10110: He walked to and fro, with thoughts very busy, until it was time to
10111: return to Tellson's and take leave of Mr. Lorry. As soon as he arrived
10112: in Paris he would present himself to this old friend, but he must say
10113: nothing of his intention now.
10114: 
10115: A carriage with post-horses was ready at the Bank door, and Jerry was
10116: booted and equipped.
10117: 
10118: "I have delivered that letter," said Charles Darnay to Mr. Lorry. "I
10119: would not consent to your being charged with any written answer, but
10120: perhaps you will take a verbal one?"
10121: 
10122: "That I will, and readily," said Mr. Lorry, "if it is not dangerous."
10123: 
10124: "Not at all. Though it is to a prisoner in the Abbaye."
10125: 
10126: "What is his name?" said Mr. Lorry, with his open pocket-book in his
10127: hand.
10128: 
10129: "Gabelle."
10130: 
10131: "Gabelle. And what is the message to the unfortunate Gabelle in prison?"
10132: 
10133: "Simply, 'that he has received the letter, and will come.'"
10134: 
10135: "Any time mentioned?"
10136: 
10137: "He will start upon his journey to-morrow night."
10138: 
10139: "Any person mentioned?"
10140: 
10141: "No."
10142: 
10143: He helped Mr. Lorry to wrap himself in a number of coats and cloaks,
10144: and went out with him from the warm atmosphere of the old Bank, into the
10145: misty air of Fleet-street. "My love to Lucie, and to little Lucie," said
10146: Mr. Lorry at parting, "and take precious care of them till I come back."
10147: Charles Darnay shook his head and doubtfully smiled, as the carriage
10148: rolled away.
10149: 
10150: That night--it was the fourteenth of August--he sat up late, and wrote
10151: two fervent letters; one was to Lucie, explaining the strong obligation
10152: he was under to go to Paris, and showing her, at length, the reasons
10153: that he had, for feeling confident that he could become involved in no
10154: personal danger there; the other was to the Doctor, confiding Lucie and
10155: their dear child to his care, and dwelling on the same topics with the
10156: strongest assurances. To both, he wrote that he would despatch letters
10157: in proof of his safety, immediately after his arrival.
10158: 
10159: It was a hard day, that day of being among them, with the first
10160: reservation of their joint lives on his mind. It was a hard matter to
10161: preserve the innocent deceit of which they were profoundly unsuspicious.
10162: But, an affectionate glance at his wife, so happy and busy, made him
10163: resolute not to tell her what impended (he had been half moved to do it,
10164: so strange it was to him to act in anything without her quiet aid), and
10165: the day passed quickly. Early in the evening he embraced her, and her
10166: scarcely less dear namesake, pretending that he would return by-and-bye
10167: (an imaginary engagement took him out, and he had secreted a valise
10168: of clothes ready), and so he emerged into the heavy mist of the heavy
10169: streets, with a heavier heart.
10170: 
10171: The unseen force was drawing him fast to itself, now, and all the tides
10172: and winds were setting straight and strong towards it. He left his
10173: two letters with a trusty porter, to be delivered half an hour before
10174: midnight, and no sooner; took horse for Dover; and began his journey.
10175: "For the love of Heaven, of justice, of generosity, of the honour of
10176: your noble name!" was the poor prisoner's cry with which he strengthened
10177: his sinking heart, as he left all that was dear on earth behind him, and
10178: floated away for the Loadstone Rock.
10179: 
10180: 
10181: The end of the second book.
10182: 
10183: 
10184: 
10185: 
10186: 
10187: Book the Third--the Track of a Storm
10188: 
10189: 
10190: 
10191: 
10192: I. In Secret
10193: 
10194: 
10195: The traveller fared slowly on his way, who fared towards Paris from
10196: England in the autumn of the year one thousand seven hundred and
10197: ninety-two. More than enough of bad roads, bad equipages, and bad
10198: horses, he would have encountered to delay him, though the fallen and
10199: unfortunate King of France had been upon his throne in all his glory;
10200: but, the changed times were fraught with other obstacles than
10201: these. Every town-gate and village taxing-house had its band of
10202: citizen-patriots, with their national muskets in a most explosive state
10203: of readiness, who stopped all comers and goers, cross-questioned them,
10204: inspected their papers, looked for their names in lists of their own,
10205: turned them back, or sent them on, or stopped them and laid them in
10206: hold, as their capricious judgment or fancy deemed best for the dawning
10207: Republic One and Indivisible, of Liberty, Equality, Fraternity, or
10208: Death.
10209: 
10210: A very few French leagues of his journey were accomplished, when Charles
10211: Darnay began to perceive that for him along these country roads there
10212: was no hope of return until he should have been declared a good citizen
10213: at Paris. Whatever might befall now, he must on to his journey's end.
10214: Not a mean village closed upon him, not a common barrier dropped across
10215: the road behind him, but he knew it to be another iron door in
10216: the series that was barred between him and England. The universal
10217: watchfulness so encompassed him, that if he had been taken in a net,
10218: or were being forwarded to his destination in a cage, he could not have
10219: felt his freedom more completely gone.
10220: 
10221: This universal watchfulness not only stopped him on the highway twenty
10222: times in a stage, but retarded his progress twenty times in a day, by
10223: riding after him and taking him back, riding before him and stopping him
10224: by anticipation, riding with him and keeping him in charge. He had been
10225: days upon his journey in France alone, when he went to bed tired out, in
10226: a little town on the high road, still a long way from Paris.
10227: 
10228: Nothing but the production of the afflicted Gabelle's letter from his
10229: prison of the Abbaye would have got him on so far. His difficulty at the
10230: guard-house in this small place had been such, that he felt his journey
10231: to have come to a crisis. And he was, therefore, as little surprised as
10232: a man could be, to find himself awakened at the small inn to which he
10233: had been remitted until morning, in the middle of the night.
10234: 
10235: Awakened by a timid local functionary and three armed patriots in rough
10236: red caps and with pipes in their mouths, who sat down on the bed.
10237: 
10238: "Emigrant," said the functionary, "I am going to send you on to Paris,
10239: under an escort."
10240: 
10241: "Citizen, I desire nothing more than to get to Paris, though I could
10242: dispense with the escort."
10243: 
10244: "Silence!" growled a red-cap, striking at the coverlet with the butt-end
10245: of his musket. "Peace, aristocrat!"
10246: 
10247: "It is as the good patriot says," observed the timid functionary. "You
10248: are an aristocrat, and must have an escort--and must pay for it."
10249: 
10250: "I have no choice," said Charles Darnay.
10251: 
10252: "Choice! Listen to him!" cried the same scowling red-cap. "As if it was
10253: not a favour to be protected from the lamp-iron!"
10254: 
10255: "It is always as the good patriot says," observed the functionary. "Rise
10256: and dress yourself, emigrant."
10257: 
10258: Darnay complied, and was taken back to the guard-house, where other
10259: patriots in rough red caps were smoking, drinking, and sleeping, by
10260: a watch-fire. Here he paid a heavy price for his escort, and hence he
10261: started with it on the wet, wet roads at three o'clock in the morning.
10262: 
10263: The escort were two mounted patriots in red caps and tri-coloured
10264: cockades, armed with national muskets and sabres, who rode one on either
10265: side of him.
10266: 
10267: The escorted governed his own horse, but a loose line was attached to
10268: his bridle, the end of which one of the patriots kept girded round his
10269: wrist. In this state they set forth with the sharp rain driving in their
10270: faces: clattering at a heavy dragoon trot over the uneven town pavement,
10271: and out upon the mire-deep roads. In this state they traversed without
10272: change, except of horses and pace, all the mire-deep leagues that lay
10273: between them and the capital.
10274: 
10275: They travelled in the night, halting an hour or two after daybreak, and
10276: lying by until the twilight fell. The escort were so wretchedly clothed,
10277: that they twisted straw round their bare legs, and thatched their ragged
10278: shoulders to keep the wet off. Apart from the personal discomfort of
10279: being so attended, and apart from such considerations of present danger
10280: as arose from one of the patriots being chronically drunk, and carrying
10281: his musket very recklessly, Charles Darnay did not allow the restraint
10282: that was laid upon him to awaken any serious fears in his breast; for,
10283: he reasoned with himself that it could have no reference to the merits
10284: of an individual case that was not yet stated, and of representations,
10285: confirmable by the prisoner in the Abbaye, that were not yet made.
10286: 
10287: But when they came to the town of Beauvais--which they did at eventide,
10288: when the streets were filled with people--he could not conceal from
10289: himself that the aspect of affairs was very alarming. An ominous crowd
10290: gathered to see him dismount of the posting-yard, and many voices called
10291: out loudly, "Down with the emigrant!"
10292: 
10293: He stopped in the act of swinging himself out of his saddle, and,
10294: resuming it as his safest place, said:
10295: 
10296: "Emigrant, my friends! Do you not see me here, in France, of my own
10297: will?"
10298: 
10299: "You are a cursed emigrant," cried a farrier, making at him in a
10300: furious manner through the press, hammer in hand; "and you are a cursed
10301: aristocrat!"
10302: 
10303: The postmaster interposed himself between this man and the rider's
10304: bridle (at which he was evidently making), and soothingly said, "Let him
10305: be; let him be! He will be judged at Paris."
10306: 
10307: "Judged!" repeated the farrier, swinging his hammer. "Ay! and condemned
10308: as a traitor." At this the crowd roared approval.
10309: 
10310: Checking the postmaster, who was for turning his horse's head to the
10311: yard (the drunken patriot sat composedly in his saddle looking on, with
10312: the line round his wrist), Darnay said, as soon as he could make his
10313: voice heard:
10314: 
10315: "Friends, you deceive yourselves, or you are deceived. I am not a
10316: traitor."
10317: 
10318: "He lies!" cried the smith. "He is a traitor since the decree. His life
10319: is forfeit to the people. His cursed life is not his own!"
10320: 
10321: At the instant when Darnay saw a rush in the eyes of the crowd, which
10322: another instant would have brought upon him, the postmaster turned his
10323: horse into the yard, the escort rode in close upon his horse's flanks,
10324: and the postmaster shut and barred the crazy double gates. The farrier
10325: struck a blow upon them with his hammer, and the crowd groaned; but, no
10326: more was done.
10327: 
10328: "What is this decree that the smith spoke of?" Darnay asked the
10329: postmaster, when he had thanked him, and stood beside him in the yard.
10330: 
10331: "Truly, a decree for selling the property of emigrants."
10332: 
10333: "When passed?"
10334: 
10335: "On the fourteenth."
10336: 
10337: "The day I left England!"
10338: 
10339: "Everybody says it is but one of several, and that there will be
10340: others--if there are not already--banishing all emigrants, and
10341: condemning all to death who return. That is what he meant when he said
10342: your life was not your own."
10343: 
10344: "But there are no such decrees yet?"
10345: 
10346: "What do I know!" said the postmaster, shrugging his shoulders; "there
10347: may be, or there will be. It is all the same. What would you have?"
10348: 
10349: They rested on some straw in a loft until the middle of the night, and
10350: then rode forward again when all the town was asleep. Among the many
10351: wild changes observable on familiar things which made this wild ride
10352: unreal, not the least was the seeming rarity of sleep. After long and
10353: lonely spurring over dreary roads, they would come to a cluster of poor
10354: cottages, not steeped in darkness, but all glittering with lights, and
10355: would find the people, in a ghostly manner in the dead of the night,
10356: circling hand in hand round a shrivelled tree of Liberty, or all drawn
10357: up together singing a Liberty song. Happily, however, there was sleep in
10358: Beauvais that night to help them out of it and they passed on once more
10359: into solitude and loneliness: jingling through the untimely cold and
10360: wet, among impoverished fields that had yielded no fruits of the earth
10361: that year, diversified by the blackened remains of burnt houses, and by
10362: the sudden emergence from ambuscade, and sharp reining up across their
10363: way, of patriot patrols on the watch on all the roads.
10364: 
10365: Daylight at last found them before the wall of Paris. The barrier was
10366: closed and strongly guarded when they rode up to it.
10367: 
10368: "Where are the papers of this prisoner?" demanded a resolute-looking man
10369: in authority, who was summoned out by the guard.
10370: 
10371: Naturally struck by the disagreeable word, Charles Darnay requested the
10372: speaker to take notice that he was a free traveller and French citizen,
10373: in charge of an escort which the disturbed state of the country had
10374: imposed upon him, and which he had paid for.
10375: 
10376: "Where," repeated the same personage, without taking any heed of him
10377: whatever, "are the papers of this prisoner?"
